It uses state reduction techniques to avoid combinatorial explosion.\n\n## Key Features\n\nLoom simulates the operating system's scheduler and Rust's memory model such that all possible valid behaviors are explored and tested. It runs all concurrent permutations of the provided closure.\n\n## How It Works\n\nBy default, loom runs an exhaustive check of your program's possible concurrent executions where all possible interleavings are checked, with state reduction algorithms significantly reducing the state space that must be explored.\n\n## Tool Execution\n\nLoom tests must be run separately, with `RUSTFLAGS=\"--cfg loom\"` specified, for example: `RUSTFLAGS=\"--cfg loom\" cargo test --test loom_my_struct`.\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nLoom is an implementation of techniques described in CDSChecker: Checking Concurrent Data Structures Written with C/C++ Atomics, with more detail on equivalent execution elimination and other techniques available in that paper.\n\nThe crate is maintained by the Tokio team and is available on crates.io under the MIT license.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"07493d46-1b4a-4965-807c-52893363dd27","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:38:42.875Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"db614e1e-1b28-4e64-8b87-b5451be69b90","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}

The project uses pattern search powered by ripgrep.\n\n## Ripgrep Search Parameters\n\nRipgrep (rg) is a powerful code search tool with extensive parameters. Here are some key search parameters:\n\n**File Type Filtering:**\n- Ripgrep can search specific types of files. For example, rg -tpy foo limits your search to Python files and rg -Tjs foo excludes JavaScript files from your search.\n\n**Pattern Matching:**\n- The -F flag treats your search pattern as a literal string, not a regex, which is useful when you don't want your . or * or () being treated as regex syntax.\n\n**Context and Output:**\n- Use -B [number] to include lines before the match, use -A [number] to include lines after the match, and use -C [number] to include lines both before and after the match.\n\n**Advanced Features:**\n- Ripgrep has optional support for switching its regex engine to use PCRE2, which makes it possible to use look-around and backreferences in patterns. PCRE2 support can be enabled with -P/--pcre2 or --auto-hybrid-regex.\n- Ripgrep supports searching files compressed in a common format (brotli, bzip2, gzip, lz4, lzma, xz, or zstandard) with the -z/--search-zip flag.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"29bff506-c93a-4b4a-9a70-0a5faa55f8b1","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:40:22.060Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"9f0c0b84-48ad-43cd-a6eb-64475bd7713e","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}

Tools are centralized in the `loom-tools` crate within the workspace and integrate with the state machine through a tool registry and execution framework.\n\n### Tool Catalog (7 Verified Tools)\n\n#### 1. **bash** (Shell Execution Tool)\n- **Mutating**: Yes (can modify filesystem/environment)\n- **Input Schema**:\n  - `command` (required, string): Bash command to execute\n  - `cwd` (optional, string): Working directory for command execution\n  - `timeout_secs` (optional, integer): Execution timeout in seconds (default: 60, max: 300)\n- **Output**: stdout/stderr captured\n- **Sandbox**: Yes - timeout-protected execution\n- **Max Timeout**: 300 seconds\n- **PostToolsHook**: Yes (required after bash execution for git operations)\n\n#### 2. **edit_file** (File Modification Tool)\n- **Mutating**: Yes (modifies filesystem)\n- **Input Schema**:\n  - `path` (required, string): File path to edit\n  - `edits[]` (required, array):\n    - `old_str` (string): Exact string to find and replace\n    - `new_str` (string): Replacement content\n  - `replace_all` (optional, boolean): Replace all occurrences if true\n- **Output**: Confirmation of edit success/failure\n- **Strategy**: Exact string matching (not regex-based)\n- **Related**: Uses unified diff internally; OpenAI's apply_patch tool uses similar pattern\n- **PostToolsHook**: Yes (required for committing file changes)\n\n#### 3. **read_file** (File Reading Tool)\n- **Mutating**: No (read-only)\n- **Input Schema**:\n  - `path` (required, string): File path to read\n- **Output**: File contents\n- **Use Case**: Read file contents when inspecting code or configuration\n\n#### 4. **list_files** (Directory Exploration Tool)\n- **Mutating**: No (read-only)\n- **Input Schema**:\n  - `path` (required, string): Directory path to list\n- **Output**: Directory contents\n- **Use Case**: Explore filesystem structure\n\n#### 5. **oracle** (LLM Delegation Tool - Agent-to-LLM)\n- **Mutating**: No (read-only, LLM call only)\n- **Input Schema**:\n  - `query` (required, string): Question/prompt for oracle\n  - `model` (optional, string): Specific LLM model to use\n  - `max_tokens` (optional, integer): Token limit for response\n  - `temperature` (optional, float): Sampling temperature (0-1)\n  - `system_prompt` (optional, string): Custom system prompt\n- **Output**: LLM response text\n- **Purpose**: Call another LLM as a tool for guidance, research, or planning\n- **Implementation**: Allows Claude to function-call another LLM (e.g., GPT) for specialized tasks\n- **Classification**: Agent-to-agent tool (LLM delegation pattern)\n\n#### 6. **web_search** (Web Search Tool)\n- **Mutating**: No (read-only)\n- **Input Schema**:\n  - `query` (required, string): Search query\n  - `max_results` (optional, integer): Maximum results to return\n- **Output**: Search results\n- **Use Case**: Retrieve information from the web\n\n#### 7. **code_search** (Pattern Search Tool - LLM generates ToolCall with tool name and parameters\n2. Tool registry looks up tool by name\n3. Tool function executes in isolated context\n4. Results captured (stdout/stderr/exit code)\n5. ToolResult fed back to LLM in next message turn\n6. LLM decides: respond or call another tool\n7. Max 50 tool turns per iteration (per agent.rs design)\n8.
